[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] establishes "Golf" as a second-level
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML_element#Basic_text' title='HTML element'>
[Text           ] heading
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] . Structural markup does not denote any specific rendering, but most web browsers have default styles for element formatting. Content may be further styled using
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cascading_Style_Sheets' title='Cascading Style Sheets'>
[Text           ] Cascading Style Sheets
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] (CSS).
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-49' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-49'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 49
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[End Tag        ] </dd>
[Start Tag      ] <dt>
[Text           ] Presentational markup describes the appearance of the text, regardless of its purpose
[End Tag        ] </dt>
[Start Tag      ] <dd>
[Text           ] For example
[Start Tag      ] <code class='nowrap' style>
[Text           ] &lt;b&gt;boldface&lt;/b&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] indicates that visual output devices should render "boldface" in bold text, but gives little indication what devices that are unable to do this (such as aural devices that read the text aloud) should do. In the case of both
[Start Tag      ] <code class='nowrap' style>
[Text           ] &lt;b&gt;bold&lt;/b&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] and
[Start Tag      ] <code class='nowrap' style>
[Text           ] &lt;i&gt;italic&lt;/i&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] , there are other elements that may have equivalent visual renderings but which are more semantic in nature, such as
[Start Tag      ] <code class='nowrap' style>
[Text           ] &lt;strong&gt;strong text&lt;/strong&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] and
[Start Tag      ] <code class='nowrap' style>
[Text           ] &lt;em&gt;emphasised text&lt;/em&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] respectively. It is easier to see how an aural user agent should interpret the latter two elements. However, they are not equivalent to their presentational counterparts: it would be undesirable for a screen-reader to emphasize the name of a book, for instance, but on a screen such a name would be italicized. Most presentational markup elements have become
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deprecation' title='Deprecation'>
[Text           ] deprecated
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] under the HTML 4.0 specification in favor of using
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cascading_Style_Sheets' title='Cascading Style Sheets'>
[Text           ] CSS
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] for styling.
[End Tag        ] </dd>
[Start Tag      ] <dt>
[Text           ] Hypertext markup makes parts of a document into links to other documents
[End Tag        ] </dt>
[Start Tag      ] <dd>
[Text           ] An anchor element creates a
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyperlink' title='Hyperlink'>
[Text           ] hyperlink
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] in the document and its
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] href
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] attribute sets the link's target
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uniform_Resource_Locator' title='Uniform Resource Locator' class='mw-redirect'>
[Text           ] URL
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] . For example the HTML markup,
[Start Tag      ] <code class='nowrap' style>
[Text           ] &lt;a href="http://www.google.com/"&gt;Wikipedia&lt;/a&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] , will render the word "
[Start Tag      ] <span class='plainlinks'>
[Start Tag      ] <a rel='nofollow' class='external text' href='http://www.google.com/'>
[Text           ] Wikipedia
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] " as a hyperlink. To render an image as a hyperlink, an "img" element is inserted as content into the "a" element. Like "br", "img" is an empty element with attributes but no content or closing tag.
[Start Tag      ] <code class='nowrap' style>
[Text           ] &lt;a href="http://example.org"&gt;
[Start Tag      ] <code class='nowrap' style>
[Text           ] &lt;img src="image.gif" alt="descriptive text" width="50" height="50" border="0"&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] &lt;/a&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] .
[End Tag        ] </dd>
[End Tag        ] </dl>
[Start Tag      ] <h4>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-headline' id='Attributes'>
[Text           ] Attributes
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit&section=9' title='Edit section: Attributes'>
[Text           ] edit
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </h4>
[Start Tag      ] <div class='hatnote relarticle mainarticle'>
[Text           ] Main article:
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML_attribute' title='HTML attribute'>
[Text           ] HTML attribute
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </div>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] Most of the attributes of an element are
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attribute-value_pair' title='Attribute-value pair' class='mw-redirect'>
[Text           ] name-value pairs
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] , separated by "=" and written within the start tag of an element after the element's name. The value may be enclosed in single or double quotes, although values consisting of certain characters can be left unquoted in HTML (but not XHTML) .
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-50' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-50'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 50
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-51' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-51'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 51
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[Text           ] Leaving attribute values unquoted is considered unsafe.
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-52' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-52'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 52
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[Text           ] In contrast with name-value pair attributes, there are some attributes that affect the element simply by their presence in the start tag of the element,
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-tagshtml_6-2' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-tagshtml-6'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 6
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[Text           ] like the
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] ismap
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] attribute for the
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] img
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] element.
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-53' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-53'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 53
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] There are several common attributes that may appear in many elements&nbsp;:
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <ul>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Text           ] The
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] id
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] attribute provides a document-wide unique identifier for an element. This is used to identify the element so that stylesheets can alter its presentational properties, and scripts may alter, animate or delete its contents or presentation. Appended to the URL of the page, it provides a globally unique identifier for the element, typically a sub-section of the page. For example, the ID "Attributes" in
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML#Attributes
[End Tag        ] </code>
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Text           ] The
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] class
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] attribute provides a way of classifying similar elements. This can be used for
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantics' title='Semantics'>
[Text           ] semantic
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] or presentation purposes. For example, an HTML document might semantically use the designation
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] class="notation"
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] to indicate that all elements with this class value are subordinate to the main text of the document. In presentation, such elements might be gathered together and presented as footnotes on a page instead of appearing in the place where they occur in the HTML source. Class attributes are used semantically in
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microformat' title='Microformat'>
[Text           ] microformats
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] . Multiple class values may be specified; for example
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] class="notation important"
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] puts the element into both the "notation" and the "important" classes.
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Text           ] An author may use the
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] style
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] attribute to assign presentational properties to a particular element. It is considered better practice to use an element's
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] id
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] or
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] class
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] attributes to select the element from within a stylesheet, though sometimes this can be too cumbersome for a simple, specific, or ad hoc styling.
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Text           ] The
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] title
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] attribute is used to attach subtextual explanation to an element. In most browsers this attribute is displayed as a
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tooltip' title='Tooltip'>
[Text           ] tooltip
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] .
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Text           ] The
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] lang
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] attribute identifies the natural language of the element's contents, which may be different from that of the rest of the document. For example, in an English-language document:
[Start Tag      ] <div dir='ltr' class='mw-geshi mw-code mw-content-ltr'>
[Start Tag      ] <div class='html4strict source-html4strict'>
[Start Tag      ] <pre class='de1'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='sc2'>
[Text           ] &lt;
[Start Tag      ] <span class='kw2'>
[Text           ] p
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] &gt;
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] Oh well,
[Start Tag      ] <span class='sc2'>
[Text           ] &lt;
[Start Tag      ] <span class='kw2'>
[Text           ] span
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='kw3'>
[Text           ] lang
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='sy0'>
[Text           ] =
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='st0'>
[Text           ] "fr"
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] &gt;
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] c'est la vie
[Start Tag      ] <span class='sc2'>
[Text           ] &lt;
[Start Tag      ] <span class='sy0'>
[Text           ] /
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='kw2'>
[Text           ] span
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] &gt;
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] , as they say in France.
[Start Tag      ] <span class='sc2'>
[Text           ] &lt;
[Start Tag      ] <span class='sy0'>
[Text           ] /
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='kw2'>
[Text           ] p
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] &gt;
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </pre>
[End Tag        ] </div>
[End Tag        ] </div>
[End Tag        ] </li>
[End Tag        ] </ul>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] The abbreviation element,
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] abbr
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] , can be used to demonstrate some of these attributes&nbsp;:
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <div dir='ltr' class='mw-geshi mw-code mw-content-ltr'>
[Start Tag      ] <div class='html4strict source-html4strict'>
[Start Tag      ] <pre class='de1'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='sc2'>
[Text           ] &lt;
[Start Tag      ] <span class='kw2'>
[Text           ] abbr
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='kw3'>
[Text           ] id
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='sy0'>
[Text           ] =
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='st0'>
[Text           ] "anId"
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='kw3'>
[Text           ] class
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='sy0'>
[Text           ] =
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='st0'>
[Text           ] "jargon"
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='kw3'>
[Text           ] style
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='sy0'>
[Text           ] =
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='st0'>
[Text           ] "color:purple;"
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='kw3'>
[Text           ] title
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='sy0'>
[Text           ] =
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='st0'>
[Text           ] "Hypertext Markup Language"
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] &gt;
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] HTML
[Start Tag      ] <span class='sc2'>
[Text           ] &lt;
[Start Tag      ] <span class='sy0'>
[Text           ] /
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='kw2'>
[Text           ] abbr
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] &gt;
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </pre>
[End Tag        ] </div>
[End Tag        ] </div>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] This example displays as
[Start Tag      ] <abbr id='anId' class='jargon' style='color:purple;' title='Hypertext Markup Language'>
[Text           ] HTML
[End Tag        ] </abbr>
[Text           ] ; in most browsers, pointing the cursor at the abbreviation should display the title text "Hypertext Markup Language."
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] Most elements take the language-related attribute
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] dir
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] to specify text direction, such as with "rtl" for right-to-left text in, for example,
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_language' title='Arabic language'>
[Text           ] Arabic
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] ,
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_language' title='Persian language'>
[Text           ] Persian
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] or
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_language' title='Hebrew language'>
[Text           ] Hebrew
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] .
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-54' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-54'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 54
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <h3>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-headline' id='Character_and_entity_references'>
[Text           ] Character and entity references
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit&section=10' title='Edit section: Character and entity references'>
[Text           ] edit
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </h3>
[Start Tag      ] <div class='hatnote boilerplate seealso'>
[Text           ] See also:
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_XML_and_HTML_character_entity_references' title='List of XML and HTML character entity references'>
[Text           ] List of XML and HTML character entity references
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] and
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unicode_and_HTML' title='Unicode and HTML'>
[Text           ] Unicode and HTML
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </div>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] As of version 4.0, HTML defines a set of 252
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Character_entity_reference' title='Character entity reference' class='mw-redirect'>
[Text           ] character entity references
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] and a set of 1,114,050
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numeric_character_reference' title='Numeric character reference'>
[Text           ] numeric character references
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] , both of which allow individual characters to be written via simple markup, rather than literally. A literal character and its markup counterpart are considered equivalent and are rendered identically.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] The ability to "escape" characters in this way allows for the characters
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &lt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] and
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &amp;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] (when written as
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &amp;lt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] and
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &amp;amp;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] , respectively) to be interpreted as character data, rather than markup. For example, a literal
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &lt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] normally indicates the start of a tag, and
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &amp;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] normally indicates the start of a character entity reference or numeric character reference; writing it as
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &amp;amp;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] or
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &amp;#x26;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] or
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &amp;#38;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] allows
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &amp;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] to be included in the content of an element or in the value of an attribute. The double-quote character (
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] "
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] ), when not used to quote an attribute value, must also be escaped as
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &amp;quot;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] or
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &amp;#x22;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] or
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &amp;#34;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] when it appears within the attribute value itself. Equivalently, the single-quote character (
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] '
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] ), when not used to quote an attribute value, must also be escaped as
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &amp;#x27;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] or
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &amp;#39;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] (or as
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &amp;apos;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] in HTML5 or XHTML documents
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-55' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-55'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 55
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-aposhtml_56-0' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-aposhtml-56'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 56
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[Text           ] ) when it appears within the attribute value itself. If document authors overlook the need to escape such characters, some browsers can be very forgiving and try to use context to guess their intent. The result is still invalid markup, which makes the document less accessible to other browsers and to other
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/User_agent' title='User agent'>
[Text           ] user agents
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] that may try to parse the document for
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_crawler' title='Web crawler'>
[Text           ] search and indexing
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] purposes for example.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] Escaping also allows for characters that are not easily typed, or that are not available in the document's
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Character_encoding' title='Character encoding'>
[Text           ] character encoding
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] , to be represented within element and attribute content. For example, the acute-accented
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] e
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] (
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] 
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] ), a character typically found only on Western European and South American keyboards, can be written in any HTML document as the entity reference
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &amp;eacute;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] or as the numeric references
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &amp;#xE9;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] or
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &amp;#233;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] , using characters that are available on all keyboards and are supported in all character encodings.
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unicode' title='Unicode'>
[Text           ] Unicode
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] character encodings such as
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UTF-8' title='UTF-8'>
[Text           ] UTF-8
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] are compatible with all modern browsers and allow direct access to almost all the characters of the world's writing systems.
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-57' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-57'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 57
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <h3>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-headline' id='Data_types'>
[Text           ] Data types
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit&section=11' title='Edit section: Data types'>
[Text           ] edit
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </h3>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] HTML defines several
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_type' title='Data type'>
[Text           ] data types
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] for element content, such as script data and stylesheet data, and a plethora of types for attribute values, including IDs, names, URIs, numbers, units of length, languages, media descriptors, colors, character encodings, dates and times, and so on. All of these data types are specializations of character data.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <h3>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-headline' id='Document_type_declaration'>
[Text           ] Document type declaration
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit&section=12' title='Edit section: Document type declaration'>
[Text           ] edit
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </h3>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] HTML documents are required to start with a
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Document_Type_Declaration' title='Document Type Declaration' class='mw-redirect'>
[Text           ] Document Type Declaration
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] (informally, a "doctype"). In browsers, the doctype helps to define the rendering modeparticularly whether to use
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quirks_mode' title='Quirks mode'>
[Text           ] quirks mode
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] .
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] The original purpose of the doctype was to enable parsing and validation of HTML documents by SGML tools based on the
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Document_Type_Definition' title='Document Type Definition' class='mw-redirect'>
[Text           ] Document Type Definition
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] (DTD). The DTD to which the DOCTYPE refers contains a machine-readable grammar specifying the permitted and prohibited content for a document conforming to such a DTD. Browsers, on the other hand, do not implement HTML as an application of SGML and by consequence do not read the DTD.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML5' title='HTML5'>
[Text           ] HTML5
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] does not define a DTD; therefore, in HTML5 the doctype declaration is simpler and shorter:
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-58' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-58'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 58
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <div dir='ltr' class='mw-geshi mw-code mw-content-ltr'>
[Start Tag      ] <div class='html5 source-html5'>
[Start Tag      ] <pre class='de1'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='sc0'>
[Text           ] &lt;!DOCTYPE html&gt;
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </pre>
[End Tag        ] </div>
[End Tag        ] </div>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] An example of an HTML 4 doctype
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <div dir='ltr' class='mw-geshi mw-code mw-content-ltr'>
[Start Tag      ] <div class='html4strict source-html4strict'>
[Start Tag      ] <pre class='de1'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='sc0'>
[Text           ] &lt;!DOCTYPE HTML PUBLIC "-//W3C//DTD HTML 4.01//EN" "http://www.w3.org/TR/html4/strict.dtd"&gt;
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </pre>
[End Tag        ] </div>
[End Tag        ] </div>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] This declaration references the DTD for the "strict" version of HTML 4.01. SGML-based validators read the DTD in order to properly parse the document and to perform validation. In modern browsers, a valid doctype activates standards mode as opposed to
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quirks_mode' title='Quirks mode'>
[Text           ] quirks mode
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] .
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] In addition, HTML 4.01 provides Transitional and Frameset DTDs,
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#Transitional_versus_strict'>
[Text           ] as explained below
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] . Transitional type is the most inclusive, incorporating current tags as well as older or "deprecated" tags, with the Strict DTD excluding deprecated tags. Frameset has all tags necessary to make frames on a page along with the tags included in transitional type
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-59' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-59'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 59
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <h2>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-headline' id='Semantic_HTML'>
[Text           ] Semantic HTML
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit&section=13' title='Edit section: Semantic HTML'>
[Text           ] edit
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </h2>
[Start Tag      ] <div class='hatnote relarticle mainarticle'>
[Text           ] Main article:
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantic_HTML' title='Semantic HTML'>
[Text           ] Semantic HTML
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </div>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] Semantic HTML is a way of writing HTML that emphasizes the meaning of the encoded information over its presentation (look). HTML has included semantic markup from its inception,
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-60' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-60'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 60
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[Text           ] but has also included presentational markup, such as
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &lt;font&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] ,
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &lt;i&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] and
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &lt;center&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] tags. There are also the semantically neutral
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Span_and_div' title='Span and div'>
[Text           ] span and div
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] tags. Since the late 1990s when
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cascading_Style_Sheets' title='Cascading Style Sheets'>
[Text           ] Cascading Style Sheets
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] were beginning to work in most browsers, web authors have been encouraged to avoid the use of presentational HTML markup with a view to the
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Separation_of_presentation_and_content' title='Separation of presentation and content'>
[Text           ] separation of presentation and content
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] .
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-61' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-61'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 61
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] In a 2001 discussion of the
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantic_Web' title='Semantic Web'>
[Text           ] Semantic Web
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] , Tim Berners-Lee and others gave examples of ways in which intelligent software "agents" may one day automatically crawl the web and find, filter and correlate previously unrelated, published facts for the benefit of human users.
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-62' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-62'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 62
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[Text           ] Such agents are not commonplace even now, but some of the ideas of
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_2.0' title='Web 2.0'>
[Text           ] Web 2.0
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] ,
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mashup_(web_application_hybrid)' title='Mashup (web application hybrid)'>
[Text           ] mashups
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] and
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Price_comparison_service' title='Price comparison service' class='mw-redirect'>
[Text           ] price comparison websites
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] may be coming close. The main difference between these web application hybrids and Berners-Lee's semantic agents lies in the fact that the current
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feed_aggregator' title='Feed aggregator' class='mw-redirect'>
[Text           ] aggregation
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] and hybridization of information is usually designed in by
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_developer' title='Web developer'>
[Text           ] web developers
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] , who already know the web locations and the
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Application_programming_interface' title='Application programming interface'>
[Text           ] API semantics
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] of the specific data they wish to mash, compare and combine.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] An important type of web agent that does crawl and read web pages automatically, without prior knowledge of what it might find, is the
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_crawler' title='Web crawler'>
[Text           ] web crawler
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] or search-engine spider. These software agents are dependent on the semantic clarity of web pages they find as they use various techniques and
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algorithm' title='Algorithm'>
[Text           ] algorithms
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] to read and index millions of web pages a day and provide web users with
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_search_engine' title='Web search engine'>
[Text           ] search facilities
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] without which the World Wide Web's usefulness would be greatly reduced.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] In order for search-engine spiders to be able to rate the significance of pieces of text they find in HTML documents, and also for those creating mashups and other hybrids as well as for more automated agents as they are developed, the semantic structures that exist in HTML need to be widely and uniformly applied to bring out the meaning of published text.
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-Semantic_Web_Revisted_63-0' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-Semantic_Web_Revisted-63'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 63
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] Presentational markup tags are
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deprecation' title='Deprecation'>
[Text           ] deprecated
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] in current HTML and XHTML recommendations and are illegal in HTML5.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] Good semantic HTML also improves the
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Accessibility' title='Accessibility'>
[Text           ] accessibility
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] of web documents (see also
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_Content_Accessibility_Guidelines' title='Web Content Accessibility Guidelines'>
[Text           ] Web Content Accessibility Guidelines
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] ). For example, when a screen reader or audio browser can correctly ascertain the structure of a document, it will not waste the visually impaired user's time by reading out repeated or irrelevant information when it has been marked up correctly.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <h2>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-headline' id='Delivery'>
[Text           ] Delivery
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit&section=14' title='Edit section: Delivery'>
[Text           ] edit
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </h2>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] HTML documents can be delivered by the same means as any other computer file. However, they are most often delivered either by
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypertext_Transfer_Protocol' title='Hypertext Transfer Protocol'>
[Text           ] HTTP
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] from a
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Web_server' title='Web server'>
[Text           ] web server
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] or by
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Email' title='Email'>
[Text           ] email
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] .
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <h3>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-headline' id='HTTP'>
[Text           ] HTTP
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit&section=15' title='Edit section: HTTP'>
[Text           ] edit
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </h3>
[Start Tag      ] <div class='hatnote relarticle mainarticle'>
[Text           ] Main article:
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypertext_Transfer_Protocol' title='Hypertext Transfer Protocol'>
[Text           ] Hypertext Transfer Protocol
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </div>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] The
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Wide_Web' title='World Wide Web'>
[Text           ] World Wide Web
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] is composed primarily of HTML documents transmitted from web servers to web browsers using the
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypertext_Transfer_Protocol' title='Hypertext Transfer Protocol'>
[Text           ] Hypertext Transfer Protocol
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] (HTTP). However, HTTP is used to serve images, sound, and other content, in addition to HTML. To allow the web browser to know how to handle each document it receives, other information is transmitted along with the document. This
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meta_data' title='Meta data' class='mw-redirect'>
[Text           ] meta data
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] usually includes the
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MIME_type' title='MIME type' class='mw-redirect'>
[Text           ] MIME type
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] (e.g.
[Start Tag      ] <tt>
[Text           ] text/html
[End Tag        ] </tt>
[Text           ] or
[Start Tag      ] <tt>
[Text           ] application/xhtml+xml
[End Tag        ] </tt>
[Text           ] ) and the character encoding (see
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Character_encoding_in_HTML' title='Character encoding in HTML' class='mw-redirect'>
[Text           ] Character encoding in HTML
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] ).
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] In modern browsers, the MIME type that is sent with the HTML document may affect how the document is initially interpreted. A document sent with the XHTML MIME type is expected to be
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/XML#Well-formed_documents' title='XML'>
[Text           ] well-formed
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] XML; syntax errors may cause the browser to fail to render it. The same document sent with the HTML MIME type might be displayed successfully, since some browsers are more lenient with HTML.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] The W3C recommendations state that XHTML 1.0 documents that follow guidelines set forth in the recommendation's Appendix C may be labeled with either MIME Type.
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-64' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-64'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 64
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[Text           ] XHTML 1.1 also states that XHTML 1.1 documents should
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-65' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-65'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 65
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[Text           ] be labeled with either MIME type.
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-66' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-66'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 66
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <h3>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-headline' id='HTML_e-mail'>
[Text           ] HTML e-mail
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit&section=16' title='Edit section: HTML e-mail'>
[Text           ] edit
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </h3>
[Start Tag      ] <div class='hatnote relarticle mainarticle'>
[Text           ] Main article:
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML_email' title='HTML email'>
[Text           ] HTML email
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </div>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] Most graphical email clients allow the use of a subset of HTML (often ill-defined) to provide formatting and
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semantic_web' title='Semantic web' class='mw-redirect'>
[Text           ] semantic
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] markup not available with
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plain_text' title='Plain text'>
[Text           ] plain text
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] . This may include typographic information like coloured headings, emphasized and quoted text, inline images and diagrams. Many such clients include both a
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graphical_user_interface' title='Graphical user interface'>
[Text           ] GUI
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] editor for composing HTML e-mail messages and a rendering engine for displaying them. Use of HTML in e-mail is criticized by some because of compatibility issues, because it can help disguise
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phishing' title='Phishing'>
[Text           ] phishing
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] attacks, because of accessibility issues for blind or visually impaired people, because it can confuse
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/E-Mail_spam' title='E-Mail spam' class='mw-redirect'>
[Text           ] spam
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] filters and because the message size is larger than plain text.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <h3>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-headline' id='Naming_conventions'>
[Text           ] Naming conventions
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit&section=17' title='Edit section: Naming conventions'>
[Text           ] edit
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </h3>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] The most common
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filename_extension' title='Filename extension'>
[Text           ] filename extension
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] for
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_file' title='Computer file'>
[Text           ] files
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] containing HTML is
[Start Tag      ] <tt>
[Text           ] .html
[End Tag        ] </tt>
[Text           ] . A common abbreviation of this is
[Start Tag      ] <tt>
[Text           ] .htm
[End Tag        ] </tt>
[Text           ] , which originated because some early operating systems and file systems, such as
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DOS' title='DOS'>
[Text           ] DOS
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] and the limitations imposed by
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File_Allocation_Table' title='File Allocation Table'>
[Text           ] FAT
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] data structure, limited file extensions to
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/8.3_filename' title='8.3 filename'>
[Text           ] three letters
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] .
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-67' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-67'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 67
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <h3>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-headline' id='HTML_Application'>
[Text           ] HTML Application
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit&section=18' title='Edit section: HTML Application'>
[Text           ] edit
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </h3>
[Start Tag      ] <div class='hatnote relarticle mainarticle'>
[Text           ] Main article:
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML_Application' title='HTML Application'>
[Text           ] HTML Application
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </div>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] An HTML Application (HTA; file extension ".hta") is a
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microsoft_Windows' title='Microsoft Windows'>
[Text           ] Microsoft Windows
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] application that uses HTML and Dynamic HTML in a browser to provide the application's graphical interface. A regular HTML file is confined to the
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Security_model&action=edit&redlink=1' class='new' title='Security model (page does not exist)'>
[Text           ] security model
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] of the
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Browser_security' title='Browser security'>
[Text           ] web browser's security
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] , communicating only to web servers and manipulating only webpage objects and
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTTP_cookie' title='HTTP cookie'>
[Text           ] site cookies
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] . An HTA runs as a fully trusted application and therefore has more privileges, like creation/editing/removal of files and
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Windows_Registry' title='Windows Registry'>
[Text           ] Windows Registry
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] entries. Because they operate outside the browser's security model, HTAs cannot be executed via HTTP, but must be downloaded (just like an
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/EXE' title='EXE' class='mw-redirect'>
[Text           ] EXE file
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] ) and executed from local file system.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <h2>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-headline' id='HTML4_variations'>
[Text           ] HTML4 variations
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit&section=19' title='Edit section: HTML4 variations'>
[Text           ] edit
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </h2>
[Start Tag      ] <div class='quotebox' style='float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:220px; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;'>
[Start Tag      ] <div class style='position: relative; text-align: left;'>
[Start Tag      ] <div>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] HTML is precisely what we were trying to PREVENT ever-breaking links, links going outward only, quotes you can't follow to their origins, no version management, no rights management.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[End Tag        ] </div>
[End Tag        ] </div>
[Start Tag      ] <div style='text-align: left;'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ted_Nelson' title='Ted Nelson'>
[Text           ] Ted Nelson
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-68' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-68'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 68
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[End Tag        ] </div>
[End Tag        ] </div>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] Since its inception, HTML and its associated protocols gained acceptance relatively quickly. However, no clear standards existed in the early years of the language. Though its creators originally conceived of HTML as a semantic language devoid of presentation details,
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-69' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-69'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 69
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[Text           ] practical uses pushed many presentational elements and attributes into the language, driven largely by the various browser vendors. The latest standards surrounding HTML reflect efforts to overcome the sometimes chaotic development of the language
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-70' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-70'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 70
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[Text           ] and to create a rational foundation for building both meaningful and well-presented documents. To return HTML to its role as a semantic language, the
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Wide_Web_Consortium' title='World Wide Web Consortium'>
[Text           ] W3C
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] has developed style languages such as
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cascading_Style_Sheets' title='Cascading Style Sheets'>
[Text           ] CSS
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] and
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extensible_Stylesheet_Language' title='Extensible Stylesheet Language' class='mw-redirect'>
[Text           ] XSL
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] to shoulder the burden of presentation. In conjunction, the HTML specification has slowly reined in the presentational elements.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] There are two axes differentiating various variations of HTML as currently specified: SGML-based HTML versus XML-based HTML (referred to as XHTML) on one axis, and strict versus transitional (loose) versus frameset on the other axis.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <h3>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-headline' id='SGML-based_versus_XML-based_HTML'>
[Text           ] SGML-based versus XML-based HTML
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit&section=20' title='Edit section: SGML-based versus XML-based HTML'>
[Text           ] edit
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </h3>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] One difference in the latest HTML specifications lies in the distinction between the SGML-based specification and the XML-based specification. The XML-based specification is usually called
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/XHTML' title='XHTML'>
[Text           ] XHTML
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] to distinguish it clearly from the more traditional definition. However, the root element name continues to be "html" even in the XHTML-specified HTML. The W3C intended XHTML 1.0 to be identical to HTML 4.01 except where limitations of XML over the more complex SGML require workarounds. Because XHTML and HTML are closely related, they are sometimes documented in parallel. In such circumstances, some authors
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/(X)HTML' title='(X)HTML' class='mw-redirect'>
[Text           ] conflate the two names
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] as (X)HTML or X(HTML).
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] Like HTML 4.01, XHTML 1.0 has three sub-specifications: strict, transitional and frameset.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] Aside from the different opening declarations for a document, the differences between an HTML 4.01 and XHTML 1.0 documentin each of the corresponding DTDsare largely syntactic. The underlying syntax of HTML allows many shortcuts that XHTML does not, such as elements with optional opening or closing tags, and even empty elements which must not have an end tag. By contrast, XHTML requires all elements to have an opening tag and a closing tag. XHTML, however, also introduces a new shortcut: an XHTML tag may be opened and closed within the same tag, by including a slash before the end of the tag like this:
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &lt;br/&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] . The introduction of this shorthand, which is not used in the SGML declaration for HTML 4.01, may confuse earlier software unfamiliar with this new convention. A fix for this is to include a space before closing the tag, as such:
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &lt;br /&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] .
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-71' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-71'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 71
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] To understand the subtle differences between HTML and XHTML, consider the transformation of a valid and well-formed XHTML 1.0 document that adheres to Appendix C (see below) into a valid HTML 4.01 document. To make this translation requires the following steps:
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <ol>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Start Tag      ] <b>
[Text           ] The language for an element should be specified with a
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] lang
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] attribute rather than the XHTML
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] xml:lang
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] attribute.
[End Tag        ] </b>
[Text           ] XHTML uses XML's built in language-defining functionality attribute.
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Start Tag      ] <b>
[Text           ] Remove the XML namespace (
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] xmlns=URI
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] ).
[End Tag        ] </b>
[Text           ] HTML has no facilities for namespaces.
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Start Tag      ] <b>
[Text           ] Change the document type declaration
[End Tag        ] </b>
[Text           ] from XHTML 1.0 to HTML 4.01. (see
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#Document_type_declaration'>
[Text           ] DTD section
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] for further explanation).
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Text           ] If present,
[Start Tag      ] <b>
[Text           ] remove the XML declaration.
[End Tag        ] </b>
[Text           ] (Typically this is:
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &lt;?xml version="1.0" encoding="utf-8"?&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] ).
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Start Tag      ] <b>
[Text           ] Ensure that the document's MIME type is set to
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] text/html
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] .
[End Tag        ] </b>
[Text           ] For both HTML and XHTML, this comes from the HTTP
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] Content-Type
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] header sent by the server.
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Start Tag      ] <b>
[Text           ] Change the XML empty-element syntax to an HTML style empty element
[End Tag        ] </b>
[Text           ] (
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &lt;br/&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] to
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &lt;br&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] ).
[End Tag        ] </li>
[End Tag        ] </ol>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] Those are the main changes necessary to translate a document from XHTML 1.0 to HTML 4.01. To translate from HTML to XHTML would also require the addition of any omitted opening or closing tags. Whether coding in HTML or XHTML it may just be best to always include the optional tags within an HTML document rather than remembering which tags can be omitted.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] A well-formed XHTML document adheres to all the syntax requirements of XML. A valid document adheres to the content specification for XHTML, which describes the document structure.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] The W3C recommends several conventions to ensure an easy migration between HTML and XHTML (see
[Start Tag      ] <a rel='nofollow' class='external text' href='http://www.w3.org/TR/xhtml1/#guidelines'>
[Text           ] HTML Compatibility Guidelines
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] ). The following steps can be applied to XHTML 1.0 documents only:
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <ul>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Text           ] Include both
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] xml:lang
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] and
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] lang
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] attributes on any elements assigning language.
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Text           ] Use the empty-element syntax only for elements specified as empty in HTML.
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Text           ] Include an extra space in empty-element tags: for example
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &lt;br /&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] instead of
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &lt;br/&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] .
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Text           ] Include explicit close tags for elements that permit content but are left empty (for example,
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &lt;div&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &lt;/div&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] , not
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &lt;div /&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] ).
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Text           ] Omit the XML declaration.
[End Tag        ] </li>
[End Tag        ] </ul>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] By carefully following the W3C's compatibility guidelines, a user agent should be able to interpret the document equally as HTML or XHTML. For documents that are XHTML 1.0 and have been made compatible in this way, the W3C permits them to be served either as HTML (with a
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] text/html
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MIME_type' title='MIME type' class='mw-redirect'>
[Text           ] MIME type
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] ), or as XHTML (with an
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] application/xhtml+xml
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] or
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] application/xml
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] MIME type). When delivered as XHTML, browsers should use an XML parser, which adheres strictly to the XML specifications for parsing the document's contents.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <h3>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-headline' id='Transitional_versus_strict'>
[Text           ] Transitional versus strict
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit&section=21' title='Edit section: Transitional versus strict'>
[Text           ] edit
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </h3>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] HTML 4 defined three different versions of the language: Strict, Transitional (once called Loose) and Frameset. The Strict version is intended for new documents and is considered best practice, while the Transitional and Frameset versions were developed to make it easier to transition documents that conformed to older HTML specification or didn't conform to any specification to a version of HTML 4. The Transitional and Frameset versions allow for
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Presentational_markup&action=edit&redlink=1' class='new' title='Presentational markup (page does not exist)'>
[Text           ] presentational markup
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] , which is omitted in the Strict version. Instead,
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cascading_style_sheets' title='Cascading style sheets' class='mw-redirect'>
[Text           ] cascading style sheets
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] are encouraged to improve the presentation of HTML documents. Because XHTML 1 only defines an XML syntax for the language defined by HTML 4, the same differences apply to XHTML 1 as well.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] The Transitional version allows the following parts of the vocabulary, which are not included in the Strict version:
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <ul>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Start Tag      ] <b>
[Text           ] A looser content model
[End Tag        ] </b>
[Start Tag      ] <ul>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Text           ] Inline elements and plain text are allowed directly in:
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] body
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] ,
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] blockquote
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] ,
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] form
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] ,
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] noscript
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] and
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] noframes
[End Tag        ] </code>
[End Tag        ] </li>
[End Tag        ] </ul>
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Start Tag      ] <b>
[Text           ] Presentation related elements
[End Tag        ] </b>
[Start Tag      ] <ul>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Text           ] underline (
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] u
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] )(Deprecated. can confuse a visitor with a hyperlink.)
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Text           ] strike-through (
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] s
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] )
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] center
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] (Deprecated. use CSS instead.)
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] font
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] (Deprecated. use CSS instead.)
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] basefont
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] (Deprecated. use CSS instead.)
[End Tag        ] </li>
[End Tag        ] </ul>
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Start Tag      ] <b>
[Text           ] Presentation related attributes
[End Tag        ] </b>
[Start Tag      ] <ul>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] background
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] (Deprecated. use CSS instead.) and
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] bgcolor
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] (Deprecated. use CSS instead.) attributes for
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] body
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] (required element according to the W3C.) element.
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] align
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] (Deprecated. use CSS instead.) attribute on
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] div
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] ,
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] form
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] , paragraph (
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] p
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] ) and heading (
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] h1
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] ...
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] h6
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] ) elements
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] align
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] (Deprecated. use CSS instead.),
[Start Tag      ] <code>

[Start Tag      ] <code>

[Start Tag      ] <code>
