[Text           ] elements
[End Tag        ] </li>
[End Tag        ] </ul>
[End Tag        ] </li>
[End Tag        ] </ul>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] The Frameset version includes everything in the Transitional version, as well as the
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] frameset
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] element (used instead of
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] body
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] ) and the
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] frame
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] element.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <h3>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-headline' id='Frameset_versus_transitional'>
[Text           ] Frameset versus transitional
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit&section=22' title='Edit section: Frameset versus transitional'>
[Text           ] edit
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </h3>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] In addition to the above transitional differences, the frameset specifications (whether XHTML 1.0 or HTML 4.01) specify a different content model, with
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] frameset
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] replacing
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] body
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] , that contains either
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] frame
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] elements, or optionally
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] noframes
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] with a
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] body
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] .
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <h3>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-headline' id='Summary_of_specification_versions'>
[Text           ] Summary of specification versions
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit&section=23' title='Edit section: Summary of specification versions'>
[Text           ] edit
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </h3>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] As this list demonstrates, the loose versions of the specification are maintained for legacy support. However, contrary to popular misconceptions, the move to XHTML does not imply a removal of this legacy support. Rather the X in XML stands for extensible and the W3C is modularizing the entire specification and opening it up to independent extensions. The primary achievement in the move from XHTML 1.0 to XHTML 1.1 is the modularization of the entire specification. The strict version of HTML is deployed in XHTML 1.1 through a set of modular extensions to the base XHTML 1.1 specification. Likewise, someone looking for the loose (transitional) or frameset specifications will find similar extended XHTML 1.1 support (much of it is contained in the legacy or frame modules). The modularization also allows for separate features to develop on their own timetable. So for example, XHTML 1.1 will allow quicker migration to emerging XML standards such as
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MathML' title='MathML'>
[Text           ] MathML
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] (a presentational and semantic math language based on XML) and
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/XForms' title='XForms'>
[Text           ] XForms
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] a new highly advanced web-form technology to replace the existing HTML forms.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] In summary, the HTML 4 specification primarily reined in all the various HTML implementations into a single clearly written specification based on SGML. XHTML 1.0, ported this specification, as is, to the new XML defined specification. Next, XHTML 1.1 takes advantage of the extensible nature of XML and modularizes the whole specification. XHTML 2.0 was intended to be the first step in adding new features to the specification in a standards-body-based approach.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <h2>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-headline' id='HTML5_variations'>
[Text           ] HTML5 variations
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit&section=24' title='Edit section: HTML5 variations'>
[Text           ] edit
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </h2>
[Start Tag      ] <h3>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-headline' id='WhatWG_HTML_versus_HTML5'>
[Text           ] WhatWG HTML versus HTML5
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit&section=25' title='Edit section: WhatWG HTML versus HTML5'>
[Text           ] edit
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </h3>
[Start Tag      ] <div class='hatnote relarticle mainarticle'>
[Text           ] Main article:
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML5' title='HTML5'>
[Text           ] HTML5
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </div>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] The
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WHATWG' title='WHATWG'>
[Start Tag      ] <abbr title='Web Hypertext Application Technology Working Group'>
[Text           ] WhatWG
[End Tag        ] </abbr>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] considers their work as
[Start Tag      ] <i>
[Text           ] living standard
[End Tag        ] </i>
[Text           ] HTML for what constitutes the state of the art in major browser implementations by
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Inc.' title='Apple Inc.'>
[Text           ] Apple
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] (
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Safari_(web_browser)' title='Safari (web browser)'>
[Text           ] Safari
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] ),
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Google' title='Google'>
[Text           ] Google
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] (
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Google_Chrome' title='Google Chrome'>
[Text           ] Chrome
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] ),
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mozilla_Foundation' title='Mozilla Foundation'>
[Text           ] Mozilla
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] (
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Firefox' title='Firefox'>
[Text           ] Firefox
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] ),
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opera_Software' title='Opera Software'>
[Text           ] Opera
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] (
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opera_(web_browser)' title='Opera (web browser)'>
[Text           ] Opera
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] ), and others. HTML5 is specified by the HTML Working Group of the
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Wide_Web_Consortium' title='World Wide Web Consortium'>
[Text           ] W3C
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] following the W3C process. As of 2013
[Start Tag      ] <sup class='plainlinks noprint asof-tag update' style='display:none;'>
[Start Tag      ] <a class='external text' href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit'>
[Text           ] [update]
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[Text           ] both specifications are similar and mostly derived from each other, i.e., the work on HTML5 started with an older WhatWG draft, and later the WhatWG
[Start Tag      ] <i>
[Text           ] living standard
[End Tag        ] </i>
[Text           ] was based on HTML5 drafts in 2011.
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-72' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-72'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 72
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-73' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-73'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 73
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <h2>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-headline' id='Hypertext_features_not_in_HTML'>
[Text           ] Hypertext features not in HTML
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit&section=26' title='Edit section: Hypertext features not in HTML'>
[Text           ] edit
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </h2>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] HTML lacks some of the features found in earlier hypertext systems, such as
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Source_tracking' title='Source tracking'>
[Text           ] source tracking
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] ,
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fat_link' title='Fat link'>
[Text           ] fat links
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] and others.
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-74' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-74'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 74
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[Text           ] Even some hypertext features that were in early versions of HTML have been ignored by most popular web browsers until recently, such as the link element and in-browser Web page editing.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] Sometimes Web services or browser manufacturers remedy these shortcomings. For instance,
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wiki' title='Wiki'>
[Text           ] wikis
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] and
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Content_management_system' title='Content management system'>
[Text           ] content management systems
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] allow surfers to edit the Web pages they visit.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <h2>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-headline' id='WYSIWYG_editors'>
[Text           ] WYSIWYG editors
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=HTML&action=edit&section=27' title='Edit section: WYSIWYG editors'>
[Text           ] edit
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-editsection-bracket'>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </h2>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] There are some
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WYSIWYG' title='WYSIWYG'>
[Text           ] WYSIWYG
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] editors (What You See Is What You Get), in which the user lays out everything as it is to appear in the HTML document using a
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Graphical_user_interface' title='Graphical user interface'>
[Text           ] graphical user interface
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] (GUI), often similar to
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Word_processor' title='Word processor'>
[Text           ] word processors
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] . The editor renders the document rather than show the code, so authors do not require extensive knowledge of HTML.
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] The WYSIWYG editing model has been criticized,
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-75' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-75'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 75
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-76' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-76'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 76
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[Text           ] primarily because of the low quality of the generated code; there are voices advocating a change to the
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WYSIWYM' title='WYSIWYM'>
[Text           ] WYSIWYM
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] model (What You See Is What You Mean).
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <p>
[Text           ] WYSIWYG editors remain a controversial topic because of their perceived flaws such as:
[End Tag        ] </p>
[Start Tag      ] <ul>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Text           ] Relying mainly on layout as opposed to meaning, often using markup that does not convey the intended meaning but simply copies the layout.
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-77' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-77'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 77
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] ]
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </sup>
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Text           ] Often producing extremely verbose and redundant code that fails to make use of the cascading nature of HTML and
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CSS' title='CSS' class='mw-redirect'>
[Text           ] CSS
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] .
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Text           ] Often producing ungrammatical markup often called
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tag_soup' title='Tag soup'>
[Text           ] tag soup
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] or semantically incorrect markup (such as
[Start Tag      ] <code>
[Text           ] &lt;em&gt;
[End Tag        ] </code>
[Text           ] for italics).
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li>
[Text           ] As a great deal of the information in HTML documents is not in the layout, the model has been criticized for its "what you see is all you get"-nature.
[Start Tag      ] <sup id='cite_ref-78' class='reference'>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_note-78'>
[Start Tag      ] <span>
[Text           ] [
[End Tag        ] </span>

[Start Tag      ] <b>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_ref-9'>

[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='reference-text'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='citation web'>
[Text           ] Tim Berners-Lee (December 9, 1991).
[Start Tag      ] <a rel='nofollow' class='external text' href='http://lists.w3.org/Archives/Public/www-talk/1991NovDec/0020.html'>
[Text           ] "Re: SGML/HTML docs, X Browser (archived www-talk mailing list post)"
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='reference-accessdate'>
[Text           ] . Retrieved
[Start Tag      ] <span class='nowrap'>
[Text           ] June 16,
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 2007
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] .
[Start Tag      ] <q>
[Text           ] SGML is very general. HTML is a specific application of the SGML basic syntax applied to hypertext documents with simple structure.
[End Tag        ] </q>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span title='ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHTML&amp;rft.aulast=Tim+Berners-Lee&amp;rft.au=Tim+Berners-Lee&amp;rft.btitle=Re%3A+SGML%2FHTML+docs%2C+X+Browser+%28archived+www-talk+mailing+list+post%29&amp;rft.date=December+9%2C+1991&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Flists.w3.org%2FArchives%2FPublic%2Fwww-talk%2F1991NovDec%2F0020.html&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook' class='Z3988'>
[Start Tag      ] <span style='display:none;'>
[Text           ] &nbsp;
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li id='cite_note-raymond-10'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-cite-backlink'>
[Start Tag      ] <b>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_ref-raymond_10-0'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='cite-accessibility-label'>
[Text           ] Jump up
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] ^
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </b>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='reference-text'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='citation book'>
[Text           ] Raymond, Eric.
[Start Tag      ] <a rel='nofollow' class='external text' href='http://www.faqs.org/docs/artu/ietf_process.html'>
[Text           ] "IETF and the RFC Standards Process"
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] .
[Start Tag      ] <a rel='nofollow' class='external text' href='http://www.faqs.org/docs/artu/'>
[Start Tag      ] <i>
[Text           ] The Art of Unix Programming
[End Tag        ] </i>
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] .
[Start Tag      ] <q>
[Text           ] In IETF tradition, standards have to arise from experience with a working prototype implementation&nbsp; but once they become standards, code that does not conform to them is considered broken and mercilessly scrapped. ...Internet-Drafts are not specifications; software implementers and vendors are specifically barred from claiming compliance with them as if they were specifications. Internet-Drafts are focal points for discussion, usually in a working group... Once an Internet-Draft has been published with an RFC number, it is a specification to which implementers may claim conformance. It is expected that the authors of the RFC and the community at large will begin correcting the specification with field experience.
[End Tag        ] </q>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span title='ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHTML&amp;rft.atitle=IETF+and+the+RFC+Standards+Process&amp;rft.aufirst=Eric&amp;rft.aulast=Raymond&amp;rft.au=Raymond%2C+Eric&amp;rft.btitle=The+Art+of+Unix+Programming&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.faqs.org%2Fdocs%2Fartu%2F&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook' class='Z3988'>
[Start Tag      ] <span style='display:none;'>
[Text           ] &nbsp;
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li id='cite_note-html.2B-11'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-cite-backlink'>
[Start Tag      ] <b>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_ref-html.2B_11-0'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='cite-accessibility-label'>
[Text           ] Jump up
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] ^
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </b>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='reference-text'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='citation web'>
[Start Tag      ] <a rel='nofollow' class='external text' href='https://datatracker.ietf.org/public/idindex.cgi?command=id_detail&id=789'>
[Text           ] "HTML+ Internet-Draft&nbsp; Abstract"
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] .
[Start Tag      ] <q>
[Text           ] Browser writers are experimenting with extensions to HTML and it is now appropriate to draw these ideas together into a revised document format. The new format is designed to allow a gradual roll over from HTML, adding features like tables, captioned figures and fill-out forms for querying remote databases or mailing questionnaires.
[End Tag        ] </q>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span title='ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHTML&amp;rft.btitle=HTML%2B+Internet-Draft%26nbsp%3B%E2%80%94+Abstract&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fdatatracker.ietf.org%2Fpublic%2Fidindex.cgi%3Fcommand%3Did_detail%26id%3D789&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook' class='Z3988'>
[Start Tag      ] <span style='display:none;'>
[Text           ] &nbsp;
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[End Tag        ] </li>
[Start Tag      ] <li id='cite_note-12'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='mw-cite-backlink'>
[Start Tag      ] <b>
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HTML?oldformat=true#cite_ref-12'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='cite-accessibility-label'>
[Text           ] Jump up
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] ^
[End Tag        ] </a>
[End Tag        ] </b>
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='reference-text'>
[Start Tag      ] <span class='citation web'>
[Text           ] Berners-Lee, Tim; Connelly, Daniel (November 1995).
[Start Tag      ] <a rel='nofollow' class='external text' href='http://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc1866'>
[Text           ] "RFC 1866 - Hypertext Markup Language - 2.0"
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] . Internet Engineering Task Force
[Start Tag      ] <span class='reference-accessdate'>
[Text           ] . Retrieved
[Start Tag      ] <span class='nowrap'>
[Text           ] 1 December
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] 2010
[End Tag        ] </span>
[Text           ] .
[Start Tag      ] <q>
[Text           ] This document thus defines an HTML 2.0 (to distinguish it from the previous informal specifications). Future (generally upwardly compatible) versions of HTML with new features will be released with higher version numbers.

[Text           ] &nbsp;

[Text           ] This article notes that presentational HTML markup may be useful when targeting browsers "before Netscape 4.0 and Internet Explorer 4.0". See the
[Start Tag      ] <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_web_browsers' title='List of web browsers'>
[Text           ] list of web browsers
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] to confirm that these were both released in 1997.

[Start Tag      ] <a rel='nofollow' class='external text' href='http://www.w3.org/TR/xhtml1/#media'>
[Text           ] "XHTML 1.0 The Extensible HyperText Markup Language (Second Edition)"
[End Tag        ] </a>
[Text           ] . World Wide Web Consortium. 2002 [2000]
[Start Tag      ] <span class='reference-accessdate'>

[End Tag        ] </span>

[Start Tag      ] <q>
[Text           ] XHTML Documents which follow the guidelines set forth in Appendix C, "HTML Compatibility Guidelines" may be labeled with the Internet Media Type "text/html" [RFC2854], as they are compatible with most HTML browsers. Those documents, and any other document conforming to this specification, may also be labeled with the Internet Media Type "application/xhtml+xml" as defined in [RFC3236].
[End Tag        ] </q>
[End Tag        ] </span>

[Text           ] 3. SHOULD This word, or the adjective "RECOMMENDED", mean that there may exist valid reasons in particular circumstances to ignore a particular item, but the full implications must be understood and carefully weighed before choosing a different course.
